Upper North Street (Lusty's Saw Mills, conveniences for opposite sexes). Upper North Street, stables rear of "Sussex Arms." Cording Street and Morris Road, wheelwrights' workshop and private residence. Grundy Street, "Duke of Edinburgh," P.H. The drainage of many premises has also been repaired and made sound. With regard to Johnson's Buildings in Kerby Street, I had, at times, noticed bad smells when inspecting the premises, and as the smells seemed to be intermittent I resolved to make a thorough examination of the drainage and soil pipes, etc. The first tests gave somewhat unsatisfactory results, so, in company with the owner, I again tested the whole, and succeeded in convincing the owner it was desirable and necessary for a thorough reconstruction of the system to be put in hand. The soil pipes were of earthenware and were fixed internally, and were cracked in three places, allowing bad smells to be blown about the rooms in times of strong down draughts, and the drain had dropped at the foot of soil pipes under the floors, causing serious defects. The small wing of the buildings will be overhauled in the forthcoming year. In accordance with the arrangements made with the Surveyor s Department concerning drainage work on new buildings, I have been present at the different jobs in my district as occasions arose, with the inspector of works, when the drainage was under test. 203 The sanitary fittings and work above ground has been looked after by myself as before, in order that the by-laws should be observed. Railway Stations. In compliance with the Committee's orders, the railway stations in my district have been inspected, and the sanitary conveniences overhauled. West India Docks station had been recently altered, and the sanitary accommodation renewed. At Poplar station, North London Railway departure platform, the drainage and fittings were found to be in a very indifferent condition. The whole was re-arranged, redrained, trapped and ' ventilated, together with the station master's residence. New water closets, etc., were provided, and automatic flushing apparatus provided in the urinal, and at my request a louvre ventilated skylight was fixed in the roof of the public closets, as these were so dark. Coffee and Eating Houses. Some of these have been closed during the year, and new ones opened in the district. There are now 32 on the register and the register is altered and revised as occasion requires. These places are visited at intervals, and at such times attention is paid to the class of food in preparation, as far as possible. They are kept in a tolerably clean condition, and when it is necessary to serve cleansing notices, they are promptly attended to. Food I aspect ion at Wharf, dir. Aberdeen Wharf, where food is landed for transit, has been periodically visited, but nothing found to complain of. As previously stated, all tinned goods are subjected to a 10 per cent. examination on arrival. Any injured or blown tins are put by for removal by contract. The butchers' premises and market stalls are carefully inspected, sometimes during the day and at other times in the evening. 204 Wherever brawn or sausages are made and where ice safes are in use, the premises are now and again, thoroughly examined. Boned beef and bull beef is used in some of the sausage making shops, and the former is very carefully examined for any signs of disease, as in this state the meat requires examining in section. Several lots of meat, fish and fruit have been surrendered during the year. On one occasion I seized a pig's head, one of the glands of which was tuberculous, but as the butcher did not know the disease, having never seen it in his experience, and had not bought the carcase, I allowed him to surrender the head, and a strong letter of caution was, by your directions, sent to him. It was also pointed out that this disease in any part of a pig is sufficient to condemn the whole carcase. On two other occasions I had surrendered on inspection, and had destroyed some large pieces of beef which were unfit for human food. The vendors were also cautioned. At intervals consignments of damaged rice, wheat, etc., are sent into my district from the Docks to be made into poultry food, and these are watched through the process. The following is a summary of food condemned during the year and destroyed: — 2 bushels of cherries Surrendered on inspection. 3 boxes of oranges Ditto. 1 pail of whelks Ditto. 1 bushel of apples Ditto. 2 dozen of oysters Ditto. ^ sack of mussels Ditto. J box of eels Ditto. 1 pig's head Ditto. About 28 lbs. of beef Ditto. 2 sacks of mussels Surrendered voluntarily. 11 sacks of peas Ditto. 5 boxes of tomatoes Ditto. 2 boxes of skate Ditto. 1 box of haddock Ditto. 2 boxes of plaice Ditto. 5 baskets of pears Ditto. 205 Numerous small lots of damaged fruit have been dealt with in a satisfactory manner. Factory and Workshops. In three instances direct aerial communication between workshops and water closets has been altered, proper partitions and ventilated skylights being provided. Additional workshops have been found and placed on the register for regular inspection, and the register altered as required. Limewashing and cleansing have been carried out in many instances by verbal intimation only, no service of notices being required. Outworkers. The various premises where outworkers live have been visited and found in fairly good condition. Underground Bakehouse. The underground bakehouse which was not finished (respecting the alterations required) at the end of 1903, is now completed, and is in occupation by a different tenant. As the former occupier continued to carry on his business without a certificate of fitness from the Council and in defiance of the Council's notices, he was summoned and fined 20s. and 23s. costs, and an order made to discontinue carrying on work till the alterations were completed and approved by the Council. Smoke Nuisance. All observations of black smoke from the factory chimneys and shafts in the district, notified from the L.C.C., and also my own observations have been dealt with. It was not found necessary to take legal proceedings in any instances respecting the above. All notices served in connection with these observations have been attended to and met as far as possible. 206 A summons against the owner of a traction engine was taken out, the result of which is reported further on under the Public Health Act. Bakehouses. These now number 25, and have been regularly inspected during the year. The bi-annual cleansing has been carried out without any difficulty. The troughs in the undergrounds, which are now all on wheels, are frequently moved out, and the surroundings properly cleansed. This could not be done formerly owing to the troughs being a fixture. One new factory bakehouse has been added to the list, and is chiefly used for baking Passover Cakes. On several occasions I had spoken to one master-baker, a German, about letting some 2 dozen fowls run loose in his bakehouse, and causing a great nuisance. As he took little notice a letter was sent by your instructions threatening legal proceedings, and no further cause was given for complaint, the fowls being kept under proper control. The man, about whose dirty habits in his bakehouse I complained of last year, has left the district, moving away in the night, no one knows of his whereabouts, and the shop is closed. Dairies, Cowsheds, Milkshops and Slaughter Houses. These places have received their due amount of attention throughout the year. Particular notice has been paid to the dippers and receptacles for the storage of milk, especially in the small general shops, and nearly every milk pan in the district is now kept covered with a proper dust tight cover. The cowsheds, before the renewal of licenses, have been visited, and thoroughly inspected, special attention being paid to overhead beams and woodwork. The register of milkshops requires frequently altering and amending, owing to so many removals of the persons registered to sell milk. 207 In one case the renewal of a slaughter house license was again opposed by the L.C.C. inspector, because the pigs must be taken through the shop to the slaughter house. The L.C.C. Licensing Committee, however, granted the renewal. The slaughter houses have been visited at night time when killing has been in progress, and the animals examined, but nothing out of the way was discovered. I am glad to say every facility has been given me for these inspections. The number of premises as above now on the registers is: — Milkshops 92 Cowsheds 2 Slaughter Houses 3 (one for swine only) Canal Boats Arts. Canal boats have been boarded and inspected as often as opportunities were presented. These numbered 26 registered boats, and about 12 unregistered sailing barges. On two occasions I endorsed notices served by the Canal Boat Inspectors of rural districts, viz.—Uxbridge and Newport Pagnell, requiring certain work to be done to the boats "Stort" and "Kennet," to stop the tar liquor getting into the cabins. The work was done at times of my inspections in a satisfactory manner, and the counterparts of the notices were returned to the authorities. Overcrowding.—No overcrowding was discovered on any boat, although on a report received, one boat was watched for and boarded, when the report was proved to be unfounded. Utensils.—These were at all times found to be in first-class condition and very clean. The pumps, bulkheads, ventilators, etc., were found invariably in good working order. 208 The amount of water stored is very small, generally about 3 galls., and the vessel holding this is replenished as opportunity offers along the line of route. Boarding.— The masters of the boats always welcome an inspection, and never place any obstacle in the way, although at times much care has to be used in getting aboard. No case of infectious disease has occurred on any of the boats, nor illness of any kind at times of my visits. Food and Drugs Acts, 1875 to 1899. 58 samples of food of different kinds have been purchased, and submitted to the Public Analyst for analysis during the year, 10 of which were proved to be adulterated. By directions of the Committee legal proceedings were taken in each case. Many others proved to contain different preservatives in more or less quantities, but a number was found to be of the very highest quality. The nature of sample and extent of adulteration, with results of legal proceedings are set out below— Milk.— Deficient in cream, 6.6 per cent. Defendant fined £1 and 23s. costs. Butter.— Adulterated with 64.7 per cent. of foreign fat, or of margarine, the fat of which contained 25 per cent. of butter fat. Defendant fined £9 and 20s. costs. Vinegar.— Deficient in acetic acid to the extent of 12 per cent., and containing a large number of vinegar eels. Defendant fined 10s. and 23s. costs. Butter.— Adulterated with 79.4 per cent. of foreign fat, and containing 0.5 per cent. of boric acid. Defendant fined 20s. and 12s. 6d. costs. Cocoa.— Adulterated with 47 per cent. of arrowroot and sugar as a mixture. Defendant fined £2 and 23s. costs. Butter.— Adulterated with 65.5 per cent. of foreign fat, and containing 1.8 per cent. of water in excess. Defendant fined 1s. and 23s. costs. (Nominal penalty asked for.) 209 Butter.— Adulterated with 79.8 per cent. of foreign fat, and containing 0.15 per cent.. of boric acid. Defendant fined 30s. and 23s. costs. Milk.— Deficient in cream to extent of 30 per cent. Defendant fined £3 and 23s. costs. Milk.— Deficient in cream 30 per cent., and solids, not fat, 20 per cent. Defendant fined 40s. and 23s. costs. Malt Vinegar.— Containing not more than 29 per cent. of malt vinegar. Defendant fined 20s. and 23s. costs. A sample of milk was purchased by mistake a few yards within the boundary of the Borough of Hackney. It proved to be adulterated, but no action could be taken in the matter. The Medical officer of Health of the Borough was communicated with by your directions. While out sampling one Sunday morning, I found a milkman, whom I had previously cautioned, selling milk without being registered, and without having his name and address properly inscribed on his hand can, in contravention of the Act of 1899. I reported the matter to the Committee and, by their directions, proceedings were taken against the vendor. The defendant was fined 7s. and 23s. costs, and at once applied for registration. He has since changed his address on two occasions, but has been re-registered at the proper times on each occasion. L. C. C. General Powers Acts. Ice Cream Regulations. All premises where ice cream is made or sold in the district, numbering 38, have now been placed on the register, and have received periodical visits during the year. Where necessary cleansing notices have been served, and have been promptly complied with. Itinerant vendors have been spoken ??? 210 to and made acquainted with the fact, that the name and address of the maker of the ice cream on sale must be legibly displayed on the barrow. The regulation is now fairly well understood, and little trouble is experienced in this respect with the foreigners selling the article. Public House Urinals. Useful work has been accomplished under the Act in so far as compelling brewers to provide proper doors and springs to the urinals opening on to the street, for the furthering of public decency. Public Health (London) Act. An outbreak of small-pox occurred in my district early in the year involving several persons. These were promptly discovered and successfully dealt with, and the spread of the disease prevented. Four cases of enteric fever, which were notified in the district, were thoroughly investigated, and I found that each patient, some 15 days previously had partaken freely of shell fish. The cases were afterwards enquired into by the Fishmongers' Company. Legal proceedings under the above Act had to be taken against the owner of 36, Sabbarton Street, for not complying with the Council's notices to remedy a defective drain. An abatement order (21 days) was made by the magistrate, and 30s. costs allowed the Council. The nuisance was abated in the time allowed. Smoke Nuisance—Traction Engine. Legal proceedings had also to be taken against the owner of a traction engine for allowing black smoke to be emitted all along the East India Dock Road, for some 20 minutes. The smoke was of a most offensively sulphurous nature. Great difficulty was experienced in serving the warrant owing to the owner moving about the country with his engine. The magistrate remarked that 211 this sort of thing could not be tolerated, and imposed a fine of 50s and 23s. costs, mentioning if the defendant were brought up a second time the penalty would be greater. L.C.C By-Laws. Several times I had occasion to caution the owner of a large offal collecting van, for collecting fat and other offensive material in the market during prohibited hours, and for not having his van properly covered, thereby causing offensive smells in the neighbourhood of his collection. As no regard was paid to my cautions, I was compelled to take proceedings in the Police Court upon the authority of the Committee. The defendant was fined £2 and 23s. costs, and his carman 20s., and 23s. costs. This seems to have abated the nuisance. Under the by-laws I have been successful in causing several side and rear passages to dwelling houses to be substantially paved and drained which has proved a boon to the users of such passages. Where work has been executed in contravention of the Council's or L.C.C. By-laws, I have interviewed the offending parties, and an explanation with an alteration of the work has put things straight without legal proceedings being taken. I am, Sir, Your obedient Servant, JOSEPH JOHNSON, R.P.C. Cert. San. Insp. Exam. Under the Public Health (London) Act, 1891, 20 applications have been made for authority to make complaint and take legal proceedings against owners in default for not complying with the Council's orders, but with the exception of one case the several nuisances were satisfactorily abated before applying for a summons. 241, East India Dock Road.—New ventilation pipe erected or constructed not in accordance with the requirements of the London County Council's By-laws, made under Section 202 of the Metropolis Local Management Act, 1855. Under the By-laws of the London County Council, Section 16 (2), there has been no occasion to take legal proceedings, particularly in reference to removal of fish offal and other offensive matter during prohibited hours. Food and Drugs Acts. Fifty-four samples have been purchased and submitted to the Public Analyst for analysis. Two were found to be adulterated, and legal proceedings instituted by order of the Committee. A number of the samples contained various preservatives, some to a larger extent than others. The nature of samples and extent of adulteration with result of proceedings are set out below. Milk.— Deficient in solids not fat to the extent of 14 per cent. Vendor fined 20s., and 23s. costs. 216 Milk, containing a foreign ingredient, viz.:— 0.015 per cent. of formaldeheyde. Summons since withdrawn. Bakehouses. I have by your instructions made periodical inspections of the bakehouses throughout my district, 17 in number, three of which are underground; the conditions in some cases have necessitated service of intimations respecting dirty walls, flooring and utensils, also accumulation of sweepings under the troughs, and the biannual limewashing not being carried out at the time specified in the Act. Cowsheds and Slaughter Houses. Five notices were received for the renewal of licenses, the premises were duly inspected, and where any infringements of the regulations were found, intimations and notices were served, and the infringements satisfactorily abated before the licenses were granted. Cowsheds 2 Slaughter Houses 3 Milk Shops and Milk Sellers. I have by your instructions made periodical inspections of the premises where milk is sold throughout the district, with the object of detecting any infringements of the regulations in respect of means of storage, prevention of contamination, registration and cleanliness; in three instances milk sellers were cautioned as to the condition of the measures, and the caution has had the desired effect. Two measures were found to be old and worn out. Intimations were served and new ones supplied. Number of milk sellers, 34. Number of milk sellers discontinued selling milk, 9. Number of milk sellers change of ownership, 10. Number of milk sellers added to register, 6. 217 Factory and Workshops. I have, by your instructions, inspected the workshops and workplaces in the district where male labour only is employed; the number of males employed in each case being checked, and any alteration found duly reported, and entered in the register kept for that purpose. Particular attention has been given to the sanitary accommodation, cleanliness, light and ventilation, in two instances the workpeople were without W. C. accommodation, one has been fixed and the other about to be fixed. Smoke Nuisances. During the past year considerably less complaints have been received with regard to the above-named nuisances, particularly in connection with Orchard Place, where most of the shafts are situated in this division. The shafts throughout the district have been kept under special observation, and when nuisances have occurred the usual notices have been served and the nuisances satisfactorily abated. More often than not the fault has been through bad stoking. On no occasion has there been cause for a summons to be taken out. Coffee Houses, Restaurants, Private Hotels, Sausage Makers, Fried Fish Shops, &c. During the past year special supervision has been given to these premises, all of which have been inspected with regard to the cleanliness, light and ventilation, and general sanitary conditions. Limewashing in nearly every case was found necessary, particulars of which have been duly reported to the Public Health and Housing Committee. The food at each premises has been examined at each visit, and there has been no cause for complaint. Ice Cream Manufacturers and Itinerant Vendors. In accordance with your instructions all the premises where ice cream is prepared have been inspected with a view of 218 detecting any infringement of Part VIII. of the London County Council (General Powers) Act, 1902, also each itinerant vendor's barrow has been inspected and in each instance the manufacturer's name was found to be legibly fixed on the barrow. At the same time the utensils were examined and found to be, as far as possible, in a clean condition. Unsound Food—Shops and Stalls. The shops and stalls: in my district have been regularly inspected with a view of detecting unsound and unwholesome food, and in a few instances parcels of fish, meat and fruit after inspection were surrendered by the owners, who were in each case severely cautioned. During the year a few cases of fish, fruit and vegetables have been brought to the Public Health Office by tradespeople and costermongers, who have found on arrival home from market, that the articles were not of the same quality as the samples shown to them, and, on examination, were found to be totally unfit for the food of man. The goods were taken to Glaucus Street Depot and destroyed, certificates given, so that the purchasers were in a position to demand the return of their money. Riverside Wharves where Food is Stored, &c. There is only one wharf in the district where food (all tinned food) is shipped and landed, Concordia Wharf, Cold Harbour. These premises have been carefully inspected and kept under strict supervision during the past year, and during that time 697 tins (various sizes) of beef, mutton, salmon, rabbits, chicken and soup were found to be blown or otherwise damaged, and on examination proved to be unfit for human consumption, they were condemned by consent of the manager, who stated they were not intended for sale. Inspection of Schools and Board Schools. In accordance with your instructions, the whole of the schools in the district have been thoroughly inspected, particularly with respect to the drinking and domestic water supplies and the cleansing of cisterns and drinking utensils, and fully reported to the Committee. 219 Poplar Stations, East India Dock Road and Brunswick Street. In accordance with your instructions, the sanitary conveniences of the above stations have been inspected, the drains were tested, and in each case found to be defective. Reconstructions on modern principals, and in accordance with the London County Council's By-laws, have since taken place. Overcrowding. I am pleased to report that only five cases have occurred during the year, all being satisfactorily abated without recourse to Police Court proceedings. I am, Sir, Your obedient Servant, JAMES BULLOCK, Assoc. San. Inst., Sanitary Inspector, Inspector tinder the Sale of Food ami Drugs Acts, and Inspector of Canal Boats. On the 17th November last the owner of 30, Marshfield Street, Cubitt Town, was fined £2 and £1 3s. costs for causing the drain at the said premises to be so repaired as to be a nuisance and injurious to health. While inspecting work at the adjoining premises No. 29, Marshfield Street, I noticed the ground appeared to have been recently disturbed above the course of the drain—which was then obstructed. This led to further enquiries being made, when it was ascertained that certain drain repairs had been executed and covered in. With the Public Health Committee's authorisation the drain was re-exposed for your examination, when defective work was revealed. At the Police Court it was proved that the work had been done by an unskilled labourer with the knowledge and by the direction of the owner. Institute, Sanitary Inspector, Inspector under the Sale of Food and Drugs Act, and Inspector of Canal Boats. 226 Public Health Department, December 31st, 1904. To the Medical Officer of Health. Sir,— I beg to present to you my fifth Annual Report, which deals with the work carried out in factories, workshops, and among outworkers during the year 1904. Overcrowding. Eleven workrooms have been overcrowded, six in Bromley and five in Bow; in each case the nuisance was abated on serving an intimation. Sanitary Accommodation. The five premises reported last year for insufficient closet accommodation have completed the alterations. During the year two workshops have made suggested improvements, and one employer discharged the females. At one factory where the accommodation was very insufficient a large addition has been made. Railway Stations. I have inspected the lavatories in the ladies' wating rooms at the 12 railway stations in the Borough, and in several cases alterations and cleansing were carried out. Outworkers. The outworkers lists have been inspected at the premises from which work is given out, and 63 lists have been received from employers in the Borough. 149 lists have been forwarded from other Boroughs, containing the names of persons who live in Poplar. 124 lists have been sent to other Councils containing the names of persons who work for employers in Poplar. Legal Proceedings. I attended the Police Court in connection with legal proceedings against five employers for not sending in their outworkers' list as 227 required by the Factory and Workshop Act, Section 107, which resulted as follows: — Shirt and blouse maker, fined 20s., costs 23s. Tailor, fined 10s., costs 23s. Tailor, fined 10s., costs 23s. Tailor, summons withdrawn, costs 23s. Underclothing maker, summons withdrawn, costs 23s. Associate Royal Sanitary Institute, 228 Public Health Department, December 31st, 1904. REPORT OF INSPECTOR FOR HOUSES LET-INLODGINGS OR OCCUPIED BY MEMBERS OF MORE THAN ONE FAMILY. To the Medical Officer of Health. Sir,— I beg to hand you the Annual Report and detailed account of the work carried out in the Borough of Poplar, under the ByLaws for Houses let in Lodgings, or occupied by members of more than one family, for the year ended 31st December, 1904. During the period January to March, the work was carried out by Mr. H. J. Langley, and from April to December, the work was carried out by myself. Registration. Houses have been registered in several new areas, and there are 768 on the books up to the present. The number of houses registered during the year was 204; and re-registered 87. Constant attention is required in keeping the Journals and Registers up-to-date, owing to tenants moving frequently, and property changing hands. I am pleased to report that the clause added to the new by-laws allowed in September last, enabling a notice to be served for the recovery of declarations of information, proves very useful in the work of registration. Nuisances. At all times when nuisances came under my notice and could not be dealt with under the by-laws, the matter was reported to the inspector for the district to be dealt with under the Act, 229 In three cases notices had to be served on lodgers and tenants for keeping rabbits, pigeons and dogs, in living rooms, causing bad smells, and an insanitary state of affairs. Overcrowding. The major part of the overcrowding in the Borough, is practically confined to certain particular areas, and probably caused by the indifference of landlords, as to the number of people who live in the houses. These areas receive constant attention, and night visits are paid from time to time. In a few of the worst cases notices had to be served, and in others the nuisance was abated by a re-distribution of the beds. Many visits are paid to the Italians, and the dangers of overcrowding are impressed upon the tenants, and their attention drawn to the exact number of lodgers that may be permitted to use each room. Cleansing. The by-laws are becoming more and more known, and much cleansing is carried out, without having to serve notices, and in some areas where the by-laws were enforced for the first time, groups of houses have been cleansed throughout. The number of rooms cleansed during the year being 752, and washhouses, areas, rear walls, W.C.'s, 258, and passages, staircases and landings, 95.
